<chapter>
<metadata.block><metadata field="right.running.head"><value>Charities and Foundations</value></metadata></metadata.block>
<front>
<outline.name.block><label>Chapter</label><designator>31</designator><name>Charities and Foundations</name></outline.name.block>
<scope.statement.block>
<para><para.text>This chapter contains forms for use in drafting documents pertaining to the formation and management of foundations and nonprofit corporations and associations for charitable purposes, together with a discussion of legal principles and tax aspects that should be considered in drafting such documents.</para.text></para>
</scope.statement.block>

<analytical.level.body>
<section.block>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:1</designator><name>In general</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Charities" numref="1">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Charities &key;1</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|1|31:1"><para.text>Charitable organizations have been exempt from federal income taxation since 1909.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|1|31:1"><para.text>Payne-Aldrich Tariff Act &sect;38, 36 Stat. 113 (1909). Now codified as <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;501(a)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Contributions to such organizations are generally deductible for purposes of the donor&apos;s income, gift, and estate taxes.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|1|31:1"><para.text>See <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:9">&sect;31:9</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Charitable organizations that qualify for the federal exemption are also exempt from New York&apos;s franchise tax and from other state and local taxes.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|1|31:1"><para.text>See <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:16">&sect;31:16</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|1|31:1"><para.text>Qualification for this preferred status is conditioned on the organization falling precisely within the terms of the statutory definition of an exempt organization.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|1|31:1"><para.text><cite type="case">Sun-Herald Corporation v. Duggan, 73 F.2d 298 (C.C.A. 2d Cir. 1934)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|1|31:1"><para.text>See <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:9 et seq." secrange="y">&dblsect;31:9 et seq.</cite></para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> As a general rule, statutes granting exemptions are strictly construed against the taxpayer, who has the burden of showing he or she is within the exemption.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|1|31:1"><para.text><cite type="case">Canton Human Services Initiatives, Inc. v. Town of Canton, 4 Misc. 3d 413, 780 N.Y.S.2d 714 (Sup 2004)</cite>, citing <cite type="case">Symphony Space, Inc. v. Tishelman, 60 N.Y.2d 33, 466 N.Y.S.2d 677, 453 N.E.2d 1094 (1983)</cite>; <cite type="case">New York Trust Co. v. U.S., 63 Ct. Cl. 100, 1927 WL 2914 (1927)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Some courts consider charitable organizations an exception, however, and are inclined to grant exemption to any organization complying with the spirit and purpose of the exemption.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|1|31:1"><para.text>See, for example, <cite type="case">Enterprise Ry. Equipment Co. v. U.S., 142 Ct. Cl. 192, 161 F. Supp. 590 (1958)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|1|31:1"><para.text>Exemption is thus crucial for successful fundraising activities, as well as successful operations. Tax considerations will inevitably play a major role in the organization and operation of any corporation or association of a charitable nature. Many of the forms and much of the legal discussion in this chapter reflect tax considerations.</para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:2</designator><name>Charity and charitable organization defined</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Charities" numref="1">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Charities &key;1</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>The term &ldquo;charity&rdquo; is used in a popular sense to mean any act of kindness to another. In a legal sense, a &ldquo;charity&rdquo; is a gift that tends to promote the well-doing and well-being of society, generally.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>A list of the purposes for which a charitable (nonprofit) corporation may be formed is contained in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="201">N.Y. Not-for-Profit Corp. Law &sect;201</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text><cite type="case">Bob Jones University v. U.S., 461 U.S. 574, 103 S. Ct. 2017, 76 L. Ed. 2d 157, 10 Ed. Law Rep. 918 (1983)</cite>; <cite type="case">Abrams v. Richmond County S.P.C., 125 Misc. 2d 530, 479 N.Y.S.2d 624 (Sup 1984)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>For checklist of matters to be included in certificate of incorporation of nonprofit corporation for charitable purposes, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:25">&sect;31:25</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Definition of charity, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Charities" secref="1">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Charities &sect;1</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Meaning of charity, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Charities" secref="1, 2" secrange="y">Am. Jur. 2d, Charities &dblsect;1, 2</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> For purposes of this chapter, however, &ldquo;charity&rdquo; or &ldquo;charitable organization&rdquo; will be used in a special sense to designate those organizations exempt from federal taxation under <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-irc" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(c)" pararef="(3)">Section 501(c)(3) of the Internal Revenue Code</cite>.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(c)" pararef="(3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;501(c)(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>For a list of additional organizations exempt from federal income taxation, see <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(c)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;501(c)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>As to a charity&apos;s exemption from various state taxes and from federal income tax, generally, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:9 et seq." secrange="y">&dblsect;31:9 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-4000 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA), &dblpara;D-4000 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Tax-exempt organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:53 et seq." secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:53 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Included in such exempt status are corporations and other organizations organized and operated exclusively for religious, charitable, scientific, testing for public safety, literary or educational purposes; to foster certain amateur sports competitions; or for the prevention of cruelty to animals or children, no part of the net earnings of which inure to the benefit of any private shareholder or individual, and no substantial part of the activities of which is the carrying on of propaganda or otherwise attempting to influence legislation except as otherwise provided by the Internal Revenue Code,<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(h)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;501(h)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> and which does not participate in or intervene in any political campaign on behalf of any candidate for public office, including the publishing or distributing of statements.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>In New York, an organization formed to carry out a charitable purpose is usually organized as a corporation, since an unincorporated association cannot take title to real estate or to a permanent fund. <cite type="case">Mount v. Tuttle, 183 N.Y. 358, 76 N.E. 873 (1906)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>Certain testamentary dispositions to unincorporated organizations are permissible where the organization incorporates within a specified period, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-estpowerstrusts" secref="3-1.3" subref="(b)">N.Y. Est. Powers &amp; Trusts Law &sect;3-1.3(b)</cite>, or where the disposition is for a charitable purpose and is subject to court supervision. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-estpowerstrusts" secref="8-1.1">EPTL &sect;8-1.1</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>Incorporation of a charitable organization is governed by the Not-for-Profit Corporation Law. See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="101 et seq." secrange="y">N-PCL &dblsect;101 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>An association must be organized and have an organizing instrument to qualify for the federal income tax exemption. See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.501(c)(3)-1">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.501(c)(3)-1</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>As to certain unincorporated associations authorized by statute, see Social and Recreation Nonprofit Organizations <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="30:1 et seq." secrange="y">&dblsect;30:1 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>As to procedure and forms to incorporate charitable organizations, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:4 et seq." secrange="y">&dblsect;31:4 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>As to qualifying for exemption, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:9 et seq." secrange="y">&dblsect;31:9 et seq.</cite></para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text>The term &ldquo;charitable&rdquo; is used in this definition in its generally accepted legal sense and includes relief of the poor and distressed or the underprivileged; advancement of religion, education, or science; erection or maintenance of public buildings, monuments, or works; lessening of the burdens of government; and promotion of social welfare by organizations designed to accomplish any of the above purposes or to lessen neighborhood tensions, eliminate prejudice and discrimination, defend human and civil rights secured by law, or to combat community deterioration and juvenile delinquency.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|2|31:2"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.501(c)(3)-1" subref="(d)" pararef="(2)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.501(c)(3)-1(d)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="ajpof3" titlename="Liability of Nonprofit Corporation for Engaging in For-Profit Business Activities" volref="46" pageref="431">Liability of Nonprofit Corporation for Engaging in For-Profit Business Activities, 46 Am. Jur. Proof of Facts 3d 431</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:3</designator><name>Private foundation defined</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4063">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4063</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|3|31:3"><para.text>A &ldquo;private foundation&rdquo; is basically one that is not publicly supported. Most exempt entities are private foundations and are subject to various additional requirements not imposed on publicly supported organizations. The Code presumes that an exempt organization is also a private foundation unless it falls within one of the exemptions.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|3|31:3"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="508" subref="(b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;508(b)</cite>. Unless the organization notifies the IRS that it is not a private foundation, it is presumed to be one. The notification is not required of churches or any other organization with income of &dollar;5,000 or less.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="508" subref="(c)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;508(c)</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Presumption that exempt organization is private foundation, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7200">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA), &para;D-7200</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|3|31:3"><para.text>The first exemption covers the &ldquo;50 percent&rdquo; charities listed in the charitable donations section of the Tax Code: churches, schools, hospitals, and publicly supported organizations.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|3|31:3"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="170" subref="(b)" pararef="(1)" spararef="(A)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;170(b)(1)(A)</cite>. The name comes from the ability of a taxpayer to contribute up to 50&percnt; of income to these charities; contributions to other charities are limited to 30&percnt;.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Churches, schools, hospitals, etc., government supported charities and governmental units, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7203">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA), &para;D-7203</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private foundations defined, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:101">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:101</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Because the publicly supported criterion under the first exemption can be hazy, a second exemption offers a more specific test. If more than one-third of an organization&apos;s support comes from the public and not more than one-third comes from investment income, it is not a private foundation.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|3|31:3"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="509" subref="(a)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;509(a)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Broadly supported organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7204 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA), &dblpara;D-7204 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private foundations defined, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:101">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:101</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> However, the one-third support cannot come from a &ldquo;disqualified person,&rdquo; who is defined as one who is a substantial contributor to the organization, one who owns more than 20&percnt; of the stock, or one who manages the operation.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|3|31:3"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4946" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4946(a)</cite>. Family members of these persons, along with trusts, partnerships, and corporations associated with them, are included as disqualified persons.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disqualified persons with respect to private foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-8100">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA), &para;D-8100</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disqualified person transactions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:108 to 10:110" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:108 to 10:110</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> A &ldquo;substantial contributor&rdquo; is one who contributes more than &dollar;5,000 if that amount is more than 2&percnt; of the total contributions. If the organization is a trust, the creator of the trust is a substantial contributor even if his or her contribution is less than &dollar;5,000.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|3|31:3"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4946" subref="(a)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4946(a)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disqualified persons with respect to private foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-8100">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA), &para;D-8100</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disqualified person transactions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:108 to 10:110" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:108 to 10:110</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|3|31:3"><para.text>The remaining two exemptions are for organizations that operate on behalf of public charities and those engaged in testing for public safety.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|3|31:3"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="509" subref="(a)" pararef="(3), (4)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;509(a)(3), (4)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|3|31:3"><para.text>Once an organization becomes a private foundation, it remains a private foundation until it becomes a public charity or distributes all assets to a public charity. It can also transfer assets to another private foundation but must then request that the termination tax not apply.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|3|31:3"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="507" subref="(g)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;507(g)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Termination of private foundation status, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7228 to D-7231" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA), &dblpara;D-7228 to D-7231</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Termination of private foundation status, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:118">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:118</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
</section.block>
</analytical.level.body>
</analytical.level>

<outline.name.block>
<designator>B</designator><name>Form Drafting Principles</name></outline.name.block>
</front>
<analytical.level.body>
<section.block>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:4</designator><name>Incorporation of charitable organizations</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Corporations and Business Organizations" numref="3350 to 3499" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Corporations and Business Organizations &key;3350 to 3499</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text>Under the New York Not-for-Profit Corporation Law<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="101 et seq." secrange="y">N-PCL &dblsect;101 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text>The New York Not-for-Profit Corporation Law applies to a domestic corporation or to a foreign corporation that conducts activities in New York State if the corporation is formed exclusively for purposes for which a not-for-profit corporation may be organized and if no part of the assets, income, or profits of which may be distributed to, or inure to the benefit of, its members, directors, or officers unless permitted by statute. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="102">N-PCL &dblsect;102</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="103">103</cite>. Certain specified types of organizations formed under other statutes are excepted from the Law. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="103" subref="(a)">N-PCL &sect;103(a)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> (&ldquo;Law&rdquo;), one or more natural persons over the age of 18 may form a nonprofit corporation.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="401">N-PCL &sect;401</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Corporations may be formed under the Law either as a charitable corporation or a noncharitable corporation.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="201" subref="(b)">N-PCL &sect;201(b)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text>Prior to its amendment by the Non-Profit Revitalization Act of 2013, the Law provided for four types of not-for-profit corporations, Types A, B, C and D. These four types were replaced with two types, charitable and noncharitable. Any corporation formed for both charitable purposes and noncharitable purposes will be deemed a charitable corporation for purposes of the Law. A type A not-for-profit corporation formed prior to July 1, 2014 will be deemed a noncharitable corporation under the Law. A Type B or C not-for-profit corporation will be deemed a charitable corporation. A Type D corporation formed for charitable purposes will be a charitable corporation and any other Type D corporation will be deemed a noncharitable corporation. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="201">N-PCL &sect;201</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> This chapter discusses corporations categorized as charitable corporations.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text>For further discussion, see Social and Recreation Nonprofit Organizations <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="30:1 et seq." secrange="y">&dblsect;30:1 et seq.</cite></para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text>The Law specifies the powers of nonprofit corporations,<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="202">N-PCL &sect;202</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Powers and functions of corporations, generally, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="421">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;421</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> which include the power to acquire, own, sell, and invest its funds in real and personal property for its use and benefit.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="202" subref="(a)" pararef="(4) to (6)">N-PCL &dblsect;202(a)(4) to (6)</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="1307">1307</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text>See also <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="203">N-PCL &sect;203</cite> (corporation may have to obtain court approval to convey its property).</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text>The corporation may convey property to a member for a dwelling house. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="205">N-PCL &sect;205</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Any corporation that is a private foundation<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text>For definition and discussion of private foundation, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:3">&sect;31:3</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> has specific restrictions on its powers.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-estpowerstrusts" secref="8-1.8">EPTL &sect;8-1.8</cite>; <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="406">N-PCL &sect;406</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements of the Not-for-Profit Corporation Law, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="71">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;71</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text>A nonprofit corporation may only conduct a business for profit as an incident to its primary purpose.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="204">N-PCL &sect;204</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Purposes of not-for-profit corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="57, 58" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;57, 58</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> However, such activity may undermine an attempt to qualify as a tax-exempt organization<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text>For discussion of qualifying for exemption, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:10">&sect;31:10</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> or subject it to unrelated business income tax.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="511">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;511</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|4|31:4"><para.text>As to taxation of unrelated business income, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:14">&sect;31:14</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:5</designator><name>Incorporation of charitable organizations<sep/>Formal requirements</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Corporations and Business Organizations" numref="3374">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Corporations and Business Organizations &key;3374</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text>To be accepted for filing by the Department of State, the certificate of incorporation must contain certain basic statements.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="402" subref="(a)">N-PCL &sect;402(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text>For contents of the certificate, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:25">&sect;31:25</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements of the Not-for-Profit Corporation Law, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="71">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;71</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The certificate must be in English, except that the corporate name may be in another language if written in English letters or characters.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="104" subref="(a)">N-PCL &sect;104(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements of the Not-for-Profit Corporation Law, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="71">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;71</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The incorporators are required to comply with certain formalities as to the signing and filing of the certificate of incorporation. The certificate must be signed by each incorporator, with each incorporator&apos;s name and address included in the certificate.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="402" subref="(a)">N-PCL &sect;402(a)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> The completed certificate must be delivered to the Department of State, together with any filing fees.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="402" subref="(a)">N-PCL &sect;402(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text>For a listing of filing fees, see <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="104-A">N.Y. Not-for-Profit Corp. Law &sect;104-A</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements of the Not-for-Profit Corporation Law, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="71">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;71</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text>If the certificate is for the incorporation of an existing unincorporated association, an affidavit of the subscribers of the certificate must be attached to the certificate stating that they constitute a majority of the members of a committee duly authorized to incorporate the association.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="402" subref="(b)">N-PCL &sect;402(b)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements of the Not-for-Profit Corporation Law, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="71">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;71</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text>Provisions regarding the particular authority that gives approvals and consents that are required to appear on certificates of incorporation for not-for-profit corporations vary according to the purpose of the corporation and are set forth by statute.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="404" subref="(a) to (v)">N-PCL &sect;404(a) to (v)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements of the Not-for-Profit Corporation Law, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="71">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;71</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Not-for-profit corporations requiring administrative approval of certificate, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="77">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;77</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text>In drafting the purpose clause for the certificate of incorporation, care should be taken to insure that this clause is sufficiently specific to qualify the corporation for exemption from federal income taxation.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text>The certificate of incorporation of a corporation that is a private foundation is deemed to include restrictions on the corporation&apos;s right to do any of the acts that may result in excise taxes being imposed on the corporation. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="406" subref="(a)">N-PCL &sect;406(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements of the Not-for-Profit Corporation Law, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="71">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;71</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Conditions imposed by statute upon exercise of powers; limitation on activities, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="423">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;423</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Purposes of not-for-profit corporations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="57, 58" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;57, 58</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text>The completed certificate must be delivered to the Department of State.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="402" subref="(a)">N-PCL &sect;402(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific requirements of the Not-for-Profit Corporation Law, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="71">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;71</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Corporate existence begins upon the filing of the certificate of incorporation by that Department.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="403">N-PCL &sect;403</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Effective date of certificate; effect of filing, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="81, 82" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;81, 82</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The corporation has perpetual existence unless otherwise specified in the certificate.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="202" subref="(a)" pararef="(1)">N-PCL &sect;202(a)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Duration, generally, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="110">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;110</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The certificate is conclusive evidence that all conditions precedent have been fulfilled and that the corporation has been formed as a not-for-profit corporation, except in an action or special proceeding brought by the Attorney General.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="403">N-PCL &sect;403</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Effect of filing, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="81, 82" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &dblsect;81, 82</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text>Securities issued by a not-for-profit corporation organized exclusively for charitable purposes are exempt from both federal and state securities registration statutes.<footnote><footnote.reference>12</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|5|31:5"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="15" secref="77c" subref="(a)" pararef="(4)">15 U.S.C.A. &sect;77c(a)(4)</cite>; <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-genbus" secref="359-f" subref="(e)">GBL &sect;359-f(e)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>

<outline.name.block>
<designator>C</designator><name>Requirements as to Registration of and Reporting by Charitable Organizations</name></outline.name.block>
</front>
<analytical.level.body>
<section.block>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:6</designator><name>Registration requirements for purposes of soliciting funds</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Charities" numref="42">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Charities &key;42</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>With several exceptions,<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>The most notable exceptions are:</para.text>
<list list.style="para">
<list.item><name.block><designator>(1)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>charitable organizations that do not intend to solicit and receive and do not actually receive contributions in excess of &dollar;25,000 during a fiscal year and that do not carry on any fundraising activities through professional fundraisers;</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>(2)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>charitable organizations that receive allocations from another organization that is in compliance with the registration requirements, that does not actually receive contributions in excess of &dollar;25,000 in excess of that allocation, and that does not use paid fundraisers; and</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>(3)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>any organization that receives substantially all of its funding from a single governmental agency and provides reports to that agency containing substantially the same information as required by the state registration statutes. For a complete list of exempt organizations, see <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172-a">Exec. Law &sect;172-a</cite>.</para.text></para></list.item>
</list></para></footnote.body></footnote> every charitable organization that intends to solicit contributions from persons in the state or from any governmental agency must file a prescribed registration form with the Attorney General before any solicitation.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172">Exec. Law &sect;172</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>A &ldquo;charitable organization&rdquo; for purposes of the filing requirement is any benevolent, philanthropic, patriotic, or eleemosynary person or one purporting to be such or a law enforcement support organization. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="171-a" subref="(1), (11)">Exec. Law &sect;171-a(1), (11)</cite>. &ldquo;Contribution&rdquo; is the promise or grant of money or property of any kind or value, whether or not in combination with the sale of goods, services, entertainment, or any other thing of value (including a grant or other financial assistance from a government agency), except for payments by members of an organization in certain circumstances. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="171-a" subref="(2)">Exec. Law &sect;171-a(2)</cite>. &ldquo;Person&rdquo; includes any individual, organization, group, association, partnership, corporation, or any combination of such entities. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="171-a" subref="(3)">Exec. Law &sect;171-a(3)</cite>. &ldquo;Solicit&rdquo; means to directly or indirectly make a request for a contribution, whether express or implied, through any medium. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="171-a" subref="(10)">Exec. Law &sect;171-a(10)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>Professional fundraisers, commercial coventurers, and fundraising counsel are also required to register with the Attorney General. The mechanics of such registration are beyond the scope of this chapter. For statutory requirements, generally, see <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="173">Exec. Law &sect;173</cite>. There is some indication that such requirements violate the registrant&apos;s constitutional right to free speech (see <cite type="case">Riley v. National Federation of the Blind of North Carolina, Inc., 487 U.S. 781, 108 S. Ct. 2667, 101 L. Ed. 2d 669 (1988)</cite>). Such persons must file a copy of each contract with a charitable organization. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="173-a" subref="(1)">Exec. Law &sect;173-a(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Regulation of fundraising activities, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Charities" secref="83 to 93" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Charities &dblsect;83 to 93</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The information required in an application for registration is specified by statute.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172" subref="(1)">Exec. Law &sect;172(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>For a checklist of matters to be included in an application for registration of solicitation, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:27">&sect;31:27</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Registration of charitable organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Charities" secref="85">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Charities &sect;85</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Any statement filed must be signed under penalties of perjury by the President or other authorized officer and by the chief fiscal officer of the organization.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172" subref="(2)">Exec. Law &sect;172(2)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> The fee for filing the statement is specified by statute.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172" subref="(3)">Exec. Law &sect;172(3)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> A corporation that has properly registered pursuant to <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-estpowerstrusts" artref="8">Article 8 of the N.Y. Estates, Powers &amp; Trusts Law</cite> is not required to register separately but must file with the Attorney General that it is registered under Article 8 and provide all the additional documents (including any necessary additional financial filings) necessary to complete registration under the Executive Law.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172" subref="(4)">Exec. Law &sect;172(4)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Registration of charitable organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Charities" secref="85">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Charities &sect;85</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> A registration remains in effect unless it is either canceled as provided by statute, withdrawn by the organization, or the organization has failed to file the required financial report and has not remedied that failure.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172" subref="(5)">Exec. Law &sect;172(5)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Registration of charitable organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Charities" secref="85">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Charities &sect;85</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The President or other authorized officer of a charity must notify the Attorney General, under oath, within 30 days of any material change in any information required to be furnished in a registration statement.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172" subref="(6)">Exec. Law &sect;172(6)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Registration of charitable organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Charities" secref="85">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Charities &sect;85</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>In addition to the registration requirements, registered charitable organizations generally must file an annual written financial report with the Attorney General on forms prescribed by that office.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172-b">Exec. Law &sect;172-b</cite>, specifying when the reports must be audited.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Annual reporting by charitable organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Charities" secref="87">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Charities &sect;87</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Failure to file a proper report will result in the discontinuance of the organization&apos;s registration. Additionally, the organization may not file a new registration until it complies with the reporting requirement and pays a re-registration fee to the Attorney General.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172" subref="(7)">Exec. Law &sect;172(7)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Annual reporting by charitable organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Charities" secref="87">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Charities &sect;87</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The forms, financial reports, professional fundraisers&apos; contracts, and other documents filed with the Attorney General become public records, except that where such records are forms including the names, addresses or telephone numbers of contributors and amounts contributed by them, such names, addresses, and telephone numbers of contributors and amounts contributed by them shall not be a public record and shall not be subject to disclosure pursuant to Article Six of the Public Officers Law, and the attorney general shall keep such information confidential, except when authorized by a court order, and use it solely for the purpose of conducting investigations and litigation to enforce the not-for-profit corporation and religious corporation laws, the provisions of this article, Article Eight of the Estates, Powers and Trusts Law, and the attorney general&apos;s other authority to oversee charities and charitable assets.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172" subref="(8)">Exec. Law &sect;172(8)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Utilizing or exploiting registration to suggest an endorsement or approval by the state is prohibited.<footnote><footnote.reference>12</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|6|31:6"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-exec" secref="172" subref="(9)">Exec. Law &sect;172(9)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Registration of charitable organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Charities" secref="85">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Charities &sect;85</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:7</designator><name>Checklist<sep/>Matters to include in an application for registration of solicitation</name></outline.name.block>
<online.view>
<online.view.item>COL</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>NFP</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>CHK</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>FCV</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>FTR</online.view.item>
<online.view.item>EBL</online.view.item>
</online.view>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<check.list>
<list list.style="para">
<list.item><name.block><designator>1</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|7|31:7"><para.text>Name of the organization and the name or names under which it intends to solicit contributions.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>2</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|7|31:7"><para.text>The names and business, residence, or other addresses where each can regularly be found of the officers, directors, trustees, and executive personnel of the organization.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>3</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|7|31:7"><para.text>Addresses of the organization, including addresses of any offices within the state. (If the organization does not maintain a principal office in New York, include the name and address of the person having custody of its financial records).</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>4</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|7|31:7"><para.text>Statement as to where and when the organization was established, its form of organization, and its tax exempt status. The form must include a copy of the most recent letter of exemption, if any, issued by the Internal Revenue Service, the most recent communication from the Internal Revenue Service regarding any audit thereby, if any, and a copy of any organizational documents, such as the certificate of incorporation, bylaws, and amendments to those documents.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>5</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|7|31:7"><para.text>A clear description of the specific programs for which the solicited contributions will be used, and a statement as to whether those programs are in existence or planned.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>6</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|7|31:7"><para.text>Date on which the fiscal year of the organization ends.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>7</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|7|31:7"><para.text>Statement as to whether the organization is authorized by any other governmental authority to solicit contributions and whether it or any of its present officers, directors, executive personnel, or trustees are or have ever been fined or otherwise penalized or enjoined from soliciting contributions or have been found to have engaged in unlawful practices regarding solicitation of contributions or administration of charitable assets and whether its registration or license has been suspended or cancelled by any court or other governmental agency together with the identity of such courts or governmental agencies and the reasons for such fine, penalty, injunction, suspension, or cancellation.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>8</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|7|31:7"><para.text>Names and addresses of any professional fundraisers, fundraising counsel, or commercial coventurers who are acting or who have agreed to act on behalf of the organization.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>9</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|7|31:7"><para.text>A copy of the organization&apos;s annual report, if any, for the immediately preceding fiscal year.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>10</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|7|31:7"><para.text>The names and addresses of any chapters, branches, affiliates, or organizations that share in the contributions or other revenue received in the state.</para.text></para></list.item>
</list>

<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|8|31:8"><para.text>With certain exceptions,<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|8|31:8"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-estpowerstrusts" secref="8-1.4" subref="(b)">EPTL &sect;8-1.4(b)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> every trustee must file with the Attorney General, within six months after any property held by the trustee or any income therefrom is required to be applied to charitable purposes, a copy of the instrument providing for the trustee&apos;s title, powers and duties.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|8|31:8"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-estpowerstrusts" secref="8-1.4" subref="(d)">EPTL &sect;8-1.4(d)</cite>.</para.text></para>

<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|8|31:8"><para.text>In addition, every trustee must, with certain exceptions,<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|8|31:8"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-estpowerstrusts" secref="8-1.4" subref="(b)">EPTL &sect;8-1.4(b)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> file annual financial reports on forms prescribed by the Attorney General and under penalties for perjury, stating information as to the nature of assets held for charitable purposes and the administration of those assets. Every trustee is also required to file with the Attorney General and all identified current charitable beneficiaries a notice of the termination of the interest of any party in a trust that would cause all or part of the trust assets to be applied to charitable purposes or to have income therefrom so applied.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|8|31:8"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-estpowerstrusts" secref="8-1.4" subref="(f)" pararef="(1)">EPTL &sect;8-1.4(f)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>

<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|8|31:8"><para.text>Unless the filing of reports is suspended, the first report must be filed within six months after the end of the fiscal year during which the trustee becomes subject to the filing requirement.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|8|31:8"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-estpowerstrusts" secref="8-1.4" subref="(g)">EPTL &sect;8-1.4(g)</cite>.</para.text></para>
