<front>
<outline.name.block>
<designator>1</designator><name>Qualification and Application for Tax Exemption</name></outline.name.block>
</front>
<analytical.level.body>
<section.block>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:9</designator><name>In general</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>Qualification for tax-exempt status under federal law is conditioned on the applicant&apos;s falling precisely within the terms of the statutory exemption in Section 501(c)(3)<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(c)" pararef="(3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;501(c)(3)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> of the Code.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text><cite type="case">Sun-Herald Corporation v. Duggan, 73 F.2d 298 (C.C.A. 2d Cir. 1934)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>An organization operated for the primary purpose of carrying on a trade or business for profit is not exempt from taxation on the ground that all of its profits are payable to one or more organizations that are exempt from taxation. The term &ldquo;trade or business&rdquo; does not, however, include: (1) the deriving of rents from real property (and personal property leased with it), with certain exceptions; (2) any trade or business in which substantially all the work in carrying it on is performed for the organization without compensation; or (3) any trade or business which is the selling of merchandise, substantially all of which has been received by the organization as gifts or contributions. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="502">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;502</cite>. In determining the primary purpose of an organization, all of the circumstances must be considered, including the size and extent of the trade or business and the size and extent of those activities of such organization that are specified in the exemption statute. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.502-1" subref="(a)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.502-1(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>For a definition of organizations that qualify under <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(c)" pararef="(3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;501(c)(3)</cite>, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:1">&sect;31:1</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>For discussion of exempt organizations, generally, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-4000 et seq.," parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-4000 et seq.,</cite> and <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:53 et seq." secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:53 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>For federal income tax purposes, associations are generally treated as corporations as long as they possess sufficient corporate characteristics, such as limited liability, centralized management, free transferability of interests, and continuity of existence.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="301.7701-1" subref="(b)">26 C.F.R. &sect;301.7701-1(b)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>Notwithstanding the exemption from federal income taxation, generally, charitable corporations are required to file an annual information return on <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-form" numref="990">IRS Form 990</cite> and private foundations are required to file an annual information return on <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-form" numref="990-PF">IRS Form 990-PF</cite>.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6033">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6033</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>Failure to file a return where required may result in the imposition of penalties. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6652">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6652</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private foundation returns, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="S-2860 to S-2862" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;S-2860 to S-2862</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>Although private foundations are generally exempt from income tax, they are subject to special taxes and to notification and reporting requirements.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>For a discussion of the taxes on private foundations, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:19">&sect;31:19</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>Subject to certain restrictions on contributions of appreciated property and other restrictions, contributions or gifts to exempt charitable organizations are currently deductible in computing federal income,<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="170">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;170</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> estate,<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="2055">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;2055</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> and gift taxes.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="2522">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;2522</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>The New York Constitution provides that the legislature may, by general law, which cannot be repealed, exempt from taxation the property used exclusively for religious, educational, or charitable purposes and owned by any corporation organized exclusively for one or more of such purposes and not operating for profit.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-const" artref="XVI" secref="1">N.Y. Const. Art. XVI, &sect;1</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|9|31:9"><para.text>For a discussion of this exemption, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:16">&sect;31:16</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr4" titlename="Exemption from real-property taxation of residential facilities maintained by hospital for patients, staff, or others" volref="61" pageref="1105">Exemption from real-property taxation of residential facilities maintained by hospital for patients, staff, or others, 61 A.L.R.4th 1105</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Tax exemption of property of educational body as extending to property used by personnel as living quarters" volref="55" pageref="485">Tax exemption of property of educational body as extending to property used by personnel as living quarters, 55 A.L.R.3d 485</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Taxation: exemption of parsonage or residence of minister, priest, rabbi, or other church personnel" volref="55" pageref="356">Taxation: exemption of parsonage or residence of minister, priest, rabbi, or other church personnel, 55 A.L.R.3d 356</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Prospective use for tax-exempt purposes as entitling property to tax exemption" volref="54" pageref="9">Prospective use for tax-exempt purposes as entitling property to tax exemption, 54 A.L.R.3d 9</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Receipt of pay from beneficiaries as affecting tax exemption of charitable institutions" volref="37" pageref="1191">Receipt of pay from beneficiaries as affecting tax exemption of charitable institutions, 37 A.L.R.3d 1191</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Homes for the aged as exempt from property taxation" volref="37" pageref="565">Homes for the aged as exempt from property taxation, 37 A.L.R.3d 565</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:10</designator><name>Qualification for exemption from federal income taxation</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>To qualify for exemption from federal income taxation, an organization must establish that its purpose falls within one of the statutory categories<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(c)" pararef="(3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;501(c)(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Tax-exempt organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:53 et seq." secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:53 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> and that its activities demonstrably serve and are in harmony with the public interest.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="case">Bob Jones University v. U.S., 461 U.S. 574, 103 S. Ct. 2017, 76 L. Ed. 2d 157, 10 Ed. Law Rep. 918 (1983)</cite> (the tax exemption may be denied if an otherwise qualified organization practices racial discrimination); <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-ruling" numref="71-447" volref="1971-2" reporter="C.B." volpg="230">Rev. Rul. 71-447, 1971-2 C.B. 230</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> The organization must be both organized and operated exclusively for charitable purposes.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(c)" pararef="(3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;501(c)(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Form of organization, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:54">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:54</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Exempt purposes, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:56">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:56</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><ital>Organizational test</ital>. A charity is considered organized exclusively for one or more charitable purposes only when its articles of organization (certificate of incorporation, certificate of association, etc.) limit the purposes of the organization to one or more charitable purposes and do not expressly empower the organization to engage in substantial activities not in furtherance of its charitable purposes.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.501(c)(3)-1" subref="(b)" pararef="(1)" spararef="(i)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.501(c)(3)-1(b)(1)(i)</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.501(c)(3)-1" subref="(b)" pararef="(2)">(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Form of organization, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:54">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:54</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> In meeting this test, the organization&apos;s purposes, as stated in its articles of organization, may be as broad as, or more specific than, the language contained in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-irc" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(c)" pararef="(3)">Section 501(c)(3) of the Internal Revenue Code</cite>, but in no event may they be broader.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.501(c)(3)-1" subref="(b)" pararef="(1)" spararef="(ii), (iv)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.501(c)(3)-1(b)(1)(ii), (iv)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> An organization is not organized exclusively for one or more exempt purposes if its articles expressly empower it to devote more than an insubstantial part of its activities to attempting to influence legislation by propaganda or otherwise or directly or indirectly to participate in or intervene in any political campaign on behalf of or in opposition to any candidate for public office, including the publishing or distributing of statements, or to have objectives and to engage in activities that characterize it as an &ldquo;action&rdquo; organization.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.501(c)(3)-1" subref="(b)" pararef="(3)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.501(c)(3)-1(b)(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Form of organization, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:54">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:54</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Exempt purposes, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:56">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:56</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>An organization is not organized exclusively for one or more exempt purposes unless its assets are dedicated to an exempt purpose. However, an organization does not meet the organizational test if, upon dissolution, its articles or the law of the state in which it was created provides that its assets would be distributed to its members or shareholders.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.501(c)(3)-1" subref="(b)" pararef="(4)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.501(c)(3)-1(b)(4)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Form of organization, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:54">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:54</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<feature.para.block><name.block><name>Practice Tips:</name></name.block>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>To avoid any problem in obtaining the exemption, it is strongly recommended that the certificate of incorporation of all corporations seeking an exemption contain an express provision irrevocably dedicating the corporation&apos;s assets to charitable use and requiring that the assets be distributed to a corporation that will continue to use them for charitable purposes.</para.text></para>
</feature.para.block>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>In construing the articles of organization, the law of the state of creation is controlling. However, any organization contending that any terms have, under state law, a different meaning from their generally accepted meaning must establish the special meaning by clear and convincing reference to relevant court decisions opinions of the state Attorney General, or to other evidence of applicable state law.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.501(c)(3)-1" subref="(b)" pararef="(5)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.501(c)(3)-1(b)(5)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><ital>Operational test</ital>. An organization will be regarded as operated exclusively for charitable purposes when it engages primarily in activities that accomplish one or more of the exempt purposes specified in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-irc" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(c)" pararef="(3)">Section 501(c)(3) of the Internal Revenue Code</cite> and if no more than an insubstantial portion of its activities is not in furtherance of such purposes.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.501(c)(3)-1" subref="(c)" pararef="(1)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.501(c)(3)-1(c)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>An organization is not operated exclusively for one or more exempt purposes if its net earnings inure in whole or in part to the benefit of private shareholders or individuals.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.501(c)(3)-1" subref="(c)" pararef="(2)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.501(c)(3)-1(c)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private inurement, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-4040 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA)&dblpara;D-4040 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private benefit rules, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:88">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:88</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>Formerly, if an exempt organization violated the rules against private benefit, the Service&apos;s only option was to revoke its exempt status. There are now intermediate sanctions under Section 4958, which imposes excise taxes if a charitable organization transfers an excess benefit to a disqualified person.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4958">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4958</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Excise taxes on excess benefit transactions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6650 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-6650 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>An &ldquo;excess benefit transaction&rdquo; is a transaction in which an economic benefit is provided by an exempt organization to a disqualified person in excess of the consideration received.<footnote><footnote.reference>12</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4958" subref="(c)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4958(c)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Excise taxes on excess benefit transactions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6650 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA)&dblpara;D-6650 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> A &ldquo;disqualified person&rdquo; is someone who, during the five years preceding the transaction, was in a position to exercise substantial influence over the affairs of the organization. Disqualified persons also include family members and certain entities in which at least 35&percnt; of the control or beneficial interest are held by persons described in the preceding sentence.<footnote><footnote.reference>13</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4958" subref="(f)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4958(f)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Excise taxes on excess benefit transactions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6650 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-6650 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>Initially, the person receiving the benefit must pay a tax of 25&percnt; of the amount of the excess benefit.<footnote><footnote.reference>14</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4958" subref="(a)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4958(a)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> If not corrected within the prescribed period, the person must then pay a tax of 200&percnt; of the excess benefit.<footnote><footnote.reference>15</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4958" subref="(b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4958(b)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> In addition, an organization manager who knowingly participates in the excess benefit transaction must pay a tax of 10&percnt; of the excess benefit.<footnote><footnote.reference>16</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4958" subref="(a)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4958(a)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> The maximum amount of this final tax is limited to &dollar;20,000.<footnote><footnote.reference>17</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4958" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4958(d)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Persons liable for these taxes must file a Form 4720.<footnote><footnote.reference>18</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="53.6011-1" subref="(b)">26 C.F.R. &sect;53.6011-1(b)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Excise taxes on excess benefit transactions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6650 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-6650 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>Furthermore, &ldquo;action&rdquo; organizations, including organizations that have as a substantial part of their activities an attempt to influence legislation by propaganda or otherwise, organizations which participate or intervene, directly or indirectly, in any political campaign on behalf of or in opposition to any candidate for a public office if their main or primary objective or objectives may be attained only by legislation or a defeat of proposed legislation and if they advocate or campaign for the attainment of such main or primary objective or objectives as distinguished from engaging in nonpartisan analysis, study, or research, are not operated exclusively for exempt purposes within the meaning of <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-irc" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(c)" pararef="(3)">Section 501(c)(3) of the Internal Revenue Code</cite>.<footnote><footnote.reference>19</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.501(c)(3)-1" subref="(c)" pararef="(3)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.501(c)(3)-1(c)(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Political activities, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:92">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:92</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> However, such an action organization may, nevertheless, qualify as a social welfare organization under Section 501(c)(4) if it meets the requirements therein.<footnote><footnote.reference>20</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(c)" pararef="(4)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;501(c)(4)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text>Additionally, in the case of an organization operated for the primary purpose of carrying on a trade or business for profit, exemption is not allowed under <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-irc" titleref="26" secref="501">Section 501 of the Internal Revenue Code</cite> on the ground that all the profits of such organization are payable to one or more organizations exempt from taxation.<footnote><footnote.reference>21</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|10|31:10"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="502">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;502</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private inurement, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-4040 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-4040 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private benefit rules, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:88">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:88</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>

<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:11</designator><name>Application for exemption from federal income taxation</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text>A new charitable organization is not treated as exempt under Section 501(c)(3) unless and until it gives the IRS notice that it is applying for recognition of its exempt status.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="508" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;508(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Exempt organization status, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-4000">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-4000</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Application for exempt status, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:57">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:57</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Failure to give such notice causes the organization to be presumed to be a private foundation.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="508" subref="(b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;508(b)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Presumption that exempt organization is private foundation, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7200">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-7200</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The notice requirements do not apply to churches, to associations of churches, or to organizations (other than private foundations) with gross receipts not in excess of &dollar;5000.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="508" subref="(c)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;508(c)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>For a discussion of the application by a charitable organization for determination of exempt status, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-4000 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA)&dblpara;D-4000 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="ajpof3" titlename="Liability of Nonprofit Corporation for Engaging in For-Profit Business Activities" volref="46" pageref="431">Liability of Nonprofit Corporation for Engaging in For-Profit Business Activities, 46 Am. Jur. Proof of Facts 3d 431</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text>Notice is generally given by filing <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-form" numref="1023">IRS Form 1023</cite> (or, if applicable, Form 1023-EZ) within 15 months after the end of the month in which the organization was organized.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.508-1" subref="(a)" pararef="(2)" spararef="(i)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.508-1(a)(2)(i)</cite> (also providing that any requests for extension of time for the filing of such notice be submitted to the appropriate office).</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text>See also <cite type="case">National Paralegal Inst. Coalition v. C.I.R., T.C. Memo. 2005-293, T.C.M. (RIA) P 2005-293 (2005)</cite>, where the Service reviews procedural aspects of filing Form 1023.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Application by a charitable organization for determination of exempt status, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-4000 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-4000 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Application for exempt status, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:57">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:57</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text>Any organization excepted from the requirement of filing notice under Section 508(a) will be exempt from taxation under Section 501(c)(3) if it meets the requirements of that section, whether or not it files such notice. However, in order to establish the exemption with the Internal Revenue Service and receive a ruling or determination letter recognizing its exempt status, an organization excepted from the notice requirement should file proof of its exemption.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.508-1" subref="(a)" pararef="(4)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.508-1(a)(4)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text>Along with <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-form" numref="1023">IRS Form 1023</cite>, the applicant must submit certain documents establishing conformity with organizational and operational requirements.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text>For discussion of organizational and operational requirements for exemption, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:9">&sect;31:9</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text>For a checklist of the documents that should accompany the application, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:28">&sect;31:28</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text>When an organization has established its exempt status, the IRS will issue a ruling or determination letter. Such a ruling or determination letter may be issued in advance of operations if the organization can describe its proposed operations in sufficient detail to permit a conclusion that it will clearly meet the particular requirements of the section of law under which exemption is claimed.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-pub" numref="557">I.R.S. Pub. 557</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Normally, such a determination is effective as of the date the organization was formed. However, if an organization is required to alter its activities or substantially amend its charter to qualify, the ruling or determination letter is effective as of the date specified in the letter.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-pub" numref="557">I.R.S. Pub. 557</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> If a nonsubstantial amendment is made, such as correction of a clerical error in the enabling instrument or the addition of a dissolution clause, exemption is usually recognized as of the date of formation if the organization&apos;s activities before the ruling or determination are consistent with the exemption requirements.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-pub" numref="557">I.R.S. Pub. 557</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Upon obtaining recognition of exemption, the organization may file a claim for a refund of income taxes paid for the period for which its exempt status is recognized.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-pub" numref="557">I.R.S. Pub. 557</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text>Rulings and determination letters granting exemptions may be revoked. The revocation may be retroactive if the organization omitted or misstated a material fact, operated in a manner materially different from that originally represented, or engaged in a prohibited transaction.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|11|31:11"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="601.201" subref="(n)" pararef="(6)">26 C.F.R. &sect;601.201(n)(6)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Continuity of exemption, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-4002">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-4002</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>

<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:12</designator><name>Effect of exempt status; returns</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text>Unless it is also classified as a private foundation,<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4940 et seq." secrange="y">26 U.S.C.A. &dblsect;4940 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text>For definition of private foundation, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:3">&sect;31:3</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> an organization that establishes its status as a charity is exempt from income tax, except with respect to unrelated business income.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;501(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="290 et seq." secrange="y">NYTL &dblsect;290 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text>As to taxation of unrelated business income, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:14">&sect;31:14</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Notwithstanding this exemption, most charities are required to file federal annual information returns.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6033">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6033</cite> (<cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-form" numref="990">IRS Form 990</cite>).</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text>For exceptions to filing, see <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6033" subref="(a)" pararef="(3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6033(a)(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private foundation returns, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="S-2860 to S-2862" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;S-2860 to S-2862</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Failure to file these returns may result in the imposition of penalties.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6652">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6652</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text>The Code requires an exempt organization to allow public inspection of its application for exemption and its three most recent annual information returns. The exempt organization must furnish copies of these documents on request. The copies must be provided without charge, other than for the reasonable costs of copying and mailing.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6104" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6104(d)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disclosure requirements, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:58">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:58</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text>Private foundations also are required to allow public inspection of the entities&apos; tax returns.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|12|31:12"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6104" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6104(d)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:13</designator><name>Tax differences among exempt organizations</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text>The tax treatment of an exempt organization depends on the specific requirements imposed on the organization and which of the three basic classifications in which it is placed. Exempt organizations are initially divided between public charities and private foundations. Public charities include hospitals, schools, and churches. Private foundations are then divided between operating foundations and nonoperating foundations. In addition to these fundamental differences, the tax code imposes specific requirements on specific exempt entities. For example, a social club must not discriminate in membership qualifications on the basis of race, color, or religion in order to remain exempt.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="501" subref="(i)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;501(i)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Discriminatory actions of social clubs, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6607">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-6607</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Social and recreational clubs, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:75">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:75</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text>Four basic categories of difference exist among the three basic forms of exempt organizations. For some purposes, private operating foundations are treated like public charities, while for other purposes they are treated like private foundations.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text><ital>Charitable deduction limitations.</ital> The limit on contributions to a public charity is the maximum amount allowed under the Code, which is 50&percnt; of the contributor&apos;s adjusted gross income for cash contributions and 30&percnt; for property that has appreciated in value.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="170" subref="(b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;170(b)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Qualified donee charitable organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="K-2850 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA), &dblpara;K-2850 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Charitable contributions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:74">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:74</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Deductible contributions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:119 to 10:144" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:119 to 10:144</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The same limitation applies to private operating foundations. For private (nonoperating) foundations, the limit is 30&percnt; for both kinds of property. Certain other property is limited to 20&percnt; of income and the amount deducted is limited to the donor&apos;s basis in the property.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text><ital>Permitted activities</ital>. Of the three groups, a public charity is granted the most freedom as to its manner of operating. It either may operate its own activities or may make grants to other operating entities. It may also engage in lobbying activities. A private operating foundation must be at least partially engaged in operational activities in order to be a private operating foundation, while a private foundation only makes grants to others. Neither a private foundation nor a private operating foundation may engage in lobbying activities. A private foundation may not make grants in excess of stated amounts to other private foundations.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text><ital>Tax on entities</ital>. A public charity is not subject to tax on its activities except for a tax levied on the charity&apos;s unrelated business income<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="511" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;511(a)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> and a tax on excess lobbying expenditures.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4911" subref="(c)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4911(c)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text>Taxation of unrelated business income, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:14">&sect;31:14</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text>Both private foundations and private operating foundations are subject to a variety of taxes on disqualified transactions and on undistributed income. The tax starts at 2&percnt; initially and can then reach 200&percnt;. Disqualified activities include such things as self-dealing between the organization and its managers or contributors, excess investments in private corporations, jeopardy investments in general, and similar actions.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4940">26 U.S.C.A. &dblsect;4940</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4941">4941</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text>For rules on self-dealing see, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4941" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4941(d)</cite>. Self-dealing involves certain acts by a disqualified person (see <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="53.4941(d)-1" subref="(a)">26 C.F.R. &sect;53.4941(d)-1(a)</cite>). A disqualified person is defined as a substantial contributor; a foundation manager; a person who owns more than 20&percnt; of a corporation, partnership, trust, or unincorporated enterprise which is itself a substantial contributor; and/or a member of the family of any individual of the first three categories. See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4946" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4946(a)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text><ital>Distribution requirements</ital>. Public charities are not subject to any requirement as to distributions. However, an operating foundation must distribute at least 3 1/3&percnt; of the value of its investment assets, while a nonoperating foundation must distribute at least 5&percnt; of its assets.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|13|31:13"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4942">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4942</cite>. An operating foundation need pay only two-thirds of its minimum return rather than the full amount required of a nonoperating foundation.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Tax on failure to distribute income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7700 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7700 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Distribution of income by private foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:111, 10:112" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:111, 10:112</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:14</designator><name>Taxation of unrelated business income</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|14|31:14"><para.text>Under both state and federal law, charitable organizations are subject to a tax, comparable to an ordinary business tax at corporate rates, on unrelated business income.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|14|31:14"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="511">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;511</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|14|31:14"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="290 et seq." secrange="y">NYTL &dblsect;290 et seq.</cite></para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Unrelated business income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6800 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-6800 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:59">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:59</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Dividends, interest, and royalties, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:68">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:68</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Other investment income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:70">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:70</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Rents, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:71">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:71</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> An unrelated business is one, the conduct of which (aside from the need for funds) is not substantially related to the charitable function of the exempt organization.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|14|31:14"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="513">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;513</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|14|31:14"><para.text>Exception is made for businesses in which all work is performed without compensation; in which the business is carried out primarily for the convenience of members, officers, employees, students, or patients; or in which the business consists of selling merchandise substantially all of which has been received as gifts or contributions. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="513" subref="(a)" pararef="(1) to (3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;513(a)(1) to (3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Unrelated trade or business defined, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6800 to D-6804" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-6800 to D-6804</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:59">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:59</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Interest, rents, royalties, and annuities received from certain controlled corporations are also subject to the tax on unrelated business income.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|14|31:14"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="512" subref="(b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;512(b)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|14|31:14"><para.text>A &ldquo;controlled corporation&rdquo; is one in which the beneficiary organization owns 80&percnt; of the total combined voting power and at least 80&percnt; of the total number of shares of all other classes of stock. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="368" subref="(c)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;368(c)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>&ldquo;Regularly carried on&rdquo; for unrelated business income tax purposes, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6808">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-6808</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Regularity of activities, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:60">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:60</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|14|31:14"><para.text>Certain activities, such as dances, engaged in intermittently or infrequently (including annually) to raise funds are not considered unrelated businesses.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|14|31:14"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.513-1" subref="(c)" pararef="(2)" spararef="(ii), (iii)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.513-1(c)(2)(ii), (iii)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>&ldquo;Regularly carried on&rdquo; for unrelated business income tax purposes, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6808">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-6808</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Regularity of activities, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:60">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:60</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Likewise, the sale of products resulting from the performance of exempt activities does not constitute an unrelated trade or business.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|14|31:14"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.513-1" subref="(d)" pararef="(4)" spararef="(ii)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.513-1(d)(4)(ii)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|14|31:14"><para.text>Returns of unrelated business income (<cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-form" numref="990-T">IRS Form 990-T</cite>) must be filed by every otherwise exempt organization having gross income of types includable in computing unrelated taxable income in excess of &dollar;1000. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.6012-2" subref="(e)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.6012-2(e)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Substantially related trade or business for UBIT purposes, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6811">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-6811</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:15</designator><name>Taxation of unrelated debt-financed and business lease income</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text>All tax-exempt organizations are taxed on income they receive from unrelated business interests.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Unrelated business income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6800 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-6800 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:59">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:59</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Such income is subject to the tax on unrelated business income if derived from controlled corporations.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text>See <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:12">&sect;31:12</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Only the exempt function income and the investment income (interest, dividends, royalties, etc.) of the organization is free of taxes.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="511">26 U.S.C.A. &dblsect;511</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="512">512</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text>Real estate rentals fall into the nontaxable classification, but personal property rentals are taxable unless they are merely incidental to a real property lease. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="512" subref="(b)" pararef="(3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;512(b)(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:59">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:59</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Dividends, interest, and royalties, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:68">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:68</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Other investment income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:70">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:70</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Rents, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:71">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:71</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text>Any business conducted must be substantially related to the exercise of the organization&apos;s exempt function in order to avoid taxation. A business in which goods are sold or services are given is classed as an unrelated business.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="513" subref="(c)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;513(c)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Unrelated trade or business defined, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6800 to D-6804" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-6800 to D-6804</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:59">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:59</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Exceptions exists for (1) businesses where the work is performed by volunteers; (2) businesses primarily for the convenience of students or employees; and (3) businesses consisting of the sale of merchandise received as gifts or contributions.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="513" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;513(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Unrelated trade or business defined, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-6800 to D-6804" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-6800 to D-6804</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:59">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:59</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text>The definition of unrelated business income also includes income earned from debt-financed property. The nature of the income is unimportant, whether it takes the form of rents, dividends, royalties, or some other form.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="512" subref="(b)" pararef="(4)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;512(b)(4)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Unrelated debt-financed income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7000 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7000 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Debt-financed acquisitions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:77, 10:78" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:77, 10:78</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The purpose is to prevent an exempt organization from buying property on credit and paying for it out of future, untaxed income.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text>The income taxed is based on the ratio of the average acquisition debt on the property to the adjusted basis of the property in the hands of the organization.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="514" subref="(c)" pararef="(7)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;514(c)(7)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> This ratio is applied both to the gross income from the property and its expenses to determine the taxable income. Property purchased subject to a mortgage or bought on an installment basis is always debt-financed property.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.514(b)-1" subref="(a)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.514(b)-1(a)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text>Some acquisitions are exempt from this rule. These include purchases of property used in the organization&apos;s exempt function (including land near the organization&apos;s other property), annuities, low and moderate income housing, and property used in a business related to the exempt activities.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="514" subref="(c)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;514(c)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Unrelated debt-financed income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7000 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7000 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Debt-financed acquisitions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:77, 10:78" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:77, 10:78</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Special rules apply to acquisitions by an exempt educational institution.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="514" subref="(c)" pararef="(9)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;514(c)(9)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text>Exempt organizations are permitted to engage in certain limited leaseback operations where no more than 25&percnt; of the floor space is leased back to the seller and the lease is on commercially reasonable terms.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="514" subref="(c)" pararef="(9)" spararef="(G)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;514(c)(9)(G)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Leasebacks covering no more than 25&percnt; of leasable space, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7055.1">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-7055.1</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> These activities will not fall under the unrelated business income strictures.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text>In addition, certain Code restrictions on the purchase of property have been relaxed. The Code provides that a fixed price and certain participating loan restrictions must be met for a purchase not to be classed as debt-financed.<footnote><footnote.reference>12</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="514" subref="(c)" pararef="(9)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;514(c)(9)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> These will no longer apply to property acquired from financial institutions in a qualified purchase. To qualify, the exempt organization must buy the real property from a financial institution that acquired it through foreclosure. Any gain to the financial institution must be ordinary income, the amount of the seller financing cannot exceed the institution&apos;s outstanding indebtedness on the property, and the value of the maximum amount payable under any participation feature cannot exceed 30&percnt; of the total purchase price.<footnote><footnote.reference>13</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|15|31:15"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="514" subref="(c)" pararef="(9)" spararef="(H)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;514(c)(9)(H)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:16</designator><name>Exemption from state taxation</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text>A not-for-profit corporation is exempt from state franchise taxes, except as to any unrelated business tax income of the organization,<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text>As to state and federal taxation of unrelated business taxable income, generally, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:13, 31:14" secrange="y">&dblsect;31:13, 31:14</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Corporations not subject to franchise tax, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Taxation and Assessment" secref="1311">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Taxation and Assessment &sect;1311</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> if the corporation does not have any stock or shares or other certificates of ownership interests, the corporation is operated on a not-for-profit basis, and no part of the corporation&apos;s net earnings inure to the benefit of any officer, director, or member.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-ny-ccr" titleref="20" secref="1-2.11" subref="(b)" pararef="(6)">20 NYCRR &sect;1-2.11(b)(6)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text>To obtain an exemption, the corporation must file New York Taxation and Finance Form CT-247 and all IRS documents granting or denying an exemption with the Department of Taxation and Finance. The IRS determination is generally followed. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-ny-ccr" titleref="20" secref="1-2.11" subref="(b)" pararef="(6)">20 NYCRR &sect;1-2.11(b)(6)</cite>. While the income to a charitable organization is exempt from state franchise taxation, a return must nonetheless be filed with the Department of Taxation and Finance, generally, on Form CT-3. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-ny-ccr" titleref="20" secref="6-1.1">20 NYCRR &sect;6-1.1</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Not-for-profit corporations are also exempt from the New York City franchise tax to the extent their activities do not generate a profit.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="case">Pan American Athletic &amp; Social Club, Inc. v. Commissioner of Finance of City of New York, 94 A.D.2d 606, 461 N.Y.S.2d 1017 (1st Dep&apos;t 1983)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text>All property owned<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text>Ownership of the property must rest in the charitable institution to qualify for exemption. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-realproptax" secref="420-a">RPTL &sect;420-a</cite>; <cite type="case">Youth Bldg. Corp. v. Board of Assessors of Nassau County, 56 N.Y.2d 765, 452 N.Y.S.2d 18, 437 N.E.2d 277 (1982)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> by a charitable organization and that is actually and exclusively used to further the organization&apos;s charitable purpose is exempt from ad valorem property taxation.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text>There are additional exemptions for properties used for specific charitable, religious, educational, medical, and other purposes of benefit to the general public in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" artref="4">Article 4 of the Tax Law</cite> and in the Education Law.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr4" titlename="What constitutes church, religious society, or institution exempt from property tax under state constitutional or statutory provisions" volref="28" pageref="344">What constitutes church, religious society, or institution exempt from property tax under state constitutional or statutory provisions, 28 A.L.R.4th 344</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Property tax: exemption of property leased by and used for purposes of otherwise tax-exempt body" volref="55" pageref="430">Property tax: exemption of property leased by and used for purposes of otherwise tax-exempt body, 55 A.L.R.3d 430</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Comment Note: Availability of tax exemption to property held on lease from exempt owner" volref="54" pageref="402">Comment Note: Availability of tax exemption to property held on lease from exempt owner, 54 A.L.R.3d 402</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Prospective use for tax-exempt purposes as entitling property to tax exemption" volref="54" pageref="9">Prospective use for tax-exempt purposes as entitling property to tax exemption, 54 A.L.R.3d 9</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Requirements for taxation of nonprofit corporation property, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Taxation and Assessment" secref="183 to 187" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Taxation and Assessment &dblsect;183 to 187</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> To be entitled to an exemption, the corporation must be organized or conducted exclusively for charitable purposes,<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="case">Youth Bldg. Corp. v. Board of Assessors of Nassau County, 56 N.Y.2d 765, 452 N.Y.S.2d 18, 437 N.E.2d 277 (1982)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Organized for exempt purposes, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Taxation and Assessment" secref="184">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Taxation and Assessment &sect;184</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> the property must be devoted exclusively to charitable purposes,<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="case">Delancey Street Foundation, Inc. v. Board of Assessment Review and Assessors of Town of Southeast, 112 A.D.2d 132, 491 N.Y.S.2d 381 (2d Dep&apos;t 1985)</cite> (criticized on other grounds by <cite type="case">Dynamite Youth Center Foundation Inc. v. Assessor of Town of Fallsburg, Sullivan County, 207 A.D.2d 34, 620 N.Y.S.2d 566 (3d Dep&apos;t 1994)</cite>); <cite type="case">Syracuse University v. City of Syracuse, 92 A.D.2d 46, 459 N.Y.S.2d 645, 9 Ed. Law Rep. 1015 (4th Dep&apos;t 1983)</cite>; <cite type="case">Zen Center of Syracuse, Inc. v. Gamage, 94 A.D.3d 1490, 943 N.Y.S.2d 346 (4th Dep&apos;t 2012)</cite>; see also <cite type="case">Sisters of the Presentation of the Blessed Virgin Mary v.
