Van Wagenen, 223 A.D.3d 987, 202 N.Y.S.3d 814, 425 Ed. Law Rep. 950 (3d Dep&apos;t 2024), appeal dismissed, 41 N.Y.3d 990, 211 N.Y.S.3d 262, 234 N.E.3d 1054 (2024)</cite>; <cite type="case">Brookdale Physicians&apos; Dialysis Associates, Inc. v. Department of Finance of City of New York, 41 N.Y.3d 608, 215 N.Y.S.3d 51, 239 N.E.3d 157 (2024)</cite>; <cite type="case">Crouse Health System, Inc. v. City of Syracuse, 126 A.D.3d 1336, 8 N.Y.S.3d 502 (4th Dep&apos;t 2015)</cite> (the test of entitlement to tax exemption under the used exclusively clause of the Real Property Tax Law is whether the particular use is reasonably incidental to the primary or major purpose of the corporation; put differently, the determination of whether the property is used exclusively for the statutory purposes depends upon whether its primary use is in furtherance of the permitted purposes).</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Used for exempt purposes, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Taxation and Assessment" secref="185, 186" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Taxation and Assessment &dblsect;185, 186</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> and the property must be in actual use by the institution in carrying out its charitable purposes.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="case">Henry Street Settlement v. Town of Yorktown, 93 A.D.2d 855, 461 N.Y.S.2d 355 (2d Dep&apos;t 1983)</cite>; <cite type="case">Welch v. City of Utica, 107 Misc. 2d 745, 435 N.Y.S.2d 892 (Sup 1981)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Prospective use for tax-exempt purposes as entitling property to tax exemption" volref="54" pageref="9">Prospective use for tax-exempt purposes as entitling property to tax exemption, 54 A.L.R.3d 9</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Prospective use for exempt purposes, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Taxation and Assessment" secref="186">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Taxation and Assessment &sect;186</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text>Not-for-profit corporations that meet statutory or regulatory requirements also are specifically exempted from having to pay New York State sales or use taxes.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="1116">NYTL &dblsect;1116</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="1210">1210</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="1212-A">1212-A</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="1218">1218</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text>See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="1116" subref="(a)" pararef="(4)">NYTL &sect;1116(a)(4)</cite>; <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-ny-ccr" titleref="20" secref="529.7">20 NYCRR &sect;529.7</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr5" titlename="Exemption of charitable or educational organization from sales or use tax" volref="69" pageref="477">Exemption of charitable or educational organization from sales or use tax, 69 A.L.R.5th 477</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Exemption of religious organization from sales or use tax" volref="54" pageref="1204">Exemption of religious organization from sales or use tax, 54 A.L.R.3d 1204</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="secondary" normalpub="alr3" titlename="Prospective use for tax-exempt purposes as entitling property to tax exemption" volref="54" pageref="9">Prospective use for tax-exempt purposes as entitling property to tax exemption, 54 A.L.R.3d 9</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Sales and use tax exemption of religious, charitable, and educational organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Taxation and Assessment" secref="1838, 1839" secrange="y">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Taxation and Assessment &dblsect;1838, 1839</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The corporation is also exempt from the New York City vault tax,<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-nyc-admincode" secref="11-2703" subref="(4)">New York City Administrative Code &sect;11-2703(4)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> commercial rent tax,<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-nyc-admincode" secref="11-704" subref="(a)" pararef="(4)">New York City Administrative Code &sect;11-704(a)(4)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> vehicle owner&apos;s tax,<footnote><footnote.reference>12</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-nyc-admincode" secref="11-2203" subref="(6)">New York City Administrative Code &sect;11-2203(6)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> hotel room occupancy tax,<footnote><footnote.reference>13</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-nyc-admincode" secref="11-2502" subref="(e)">New York City Administrative Code &sect;11-2502(e)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> retail liquor licensee tax,<footnote><footnote.reference>14</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-nyc-admincode" secref="11-2403" subref="(d)">New York City Administrative Code &sect;11-2403(d)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> taxicab license transfer tax,<footnote><footnote.reference>15</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-nyc-admincode" secref="11-1405" subref="(a)" pararef="(4)">New York City Administrative Code &sect;11-1405(a)(4)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> and utility tax.<footnote><footnote.reference>16</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="1230" subref="(d)">NYTL &sect;1230(d)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text>A contributor or a donor of property to a corporation organized for charitable purposes is entitled to a deduction from New York&apos;s income<footnote><footnote.reference>17</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="612" subref="(a)">NYTL &sect;612(a)</cite> (the taxpayer&apos;s taxable income for state purposes does not include amounts deducted for charitable donations for federal purposes).</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> and estate taxes.<footnote><footnote.reference>18</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|16|31:16"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-tax" secref="954">NYTL &sect;954</cite> (the taxpayer&apos;s taxable estate for state purposes does not include amounts deducted for charitable donations for federal purposes).</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
</section.block>
</analytical.level.body>
</analytical.level>
<analytical.level>
<front>
<outline.name.block>
<designator>2</designator><name>Charity&apos;s Status as Private Foundation</name></outline.name.block>
</front>
<analytical.level.body>
<section.block>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:17</designator><name>Definitions<sep/>Private operating foundation; qualifying distributions; minimum investment return</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>A charitable organization that acts as a private foundation<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>For a discussion of the characteristics that make a charitable organization a private foundation, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:3">&sect;31:3</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7200 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7200 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:100 to 10:118" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:100 to 10:118</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> is exempt from taxes on its net investment income and on its undistributed income<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>For a discussion of such taxes, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:19">&sect;31:19</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> if it can establish that it is an exempt operating foundation.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4940" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &dblsect;4940(d)</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4942" subref="(a)" pararef="(1)">4942(a)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Operating foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7713 to D-7715" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7713 to D-7715</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Operating foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:116">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:116</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> A gray area exists between publicly supported organizations and private foundations that is filled by the concept of a private operating foundation. A &ldquo;private operating foundation&rdquo; is an exempt organization that is not publicly supported and is therefore a private foundation but does more than merely make grants to others.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Operating foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7713 to D-7715" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7713 to D-7715</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Operating foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:116">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:116</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> These are organizations actively engaged in exempt activities. An example would be an organization established to train teachers that actively conducts courses and seminars.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="53.4942(b)-1" subref="(d)">26 C.F.R. &sect;53.4942(b)-1(d)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>A private operating foundation is one that uses its charitable contributions for activities that it personally conducts, not just for making grants to others. The funds expended for this purpose must be substantially the entire income of the organization or its minimum investment return.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4942" subref="(j)" pararef="(3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4942(j)(3)</cite>. The Code provides that the organization must make distributions directly for the active conduct of the activities constituting the purpose or function for which it is organized.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>Operating foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:116">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:116</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>Operating foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7713 to D-7715" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7713 to D-7715</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>Two tests must be met to qualify as a private operating foundation. The first is the income test that requires the organization to spend substantially all (85&percnt;) of the lesser of its net income or its minimum investment return.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>&ldquo;Substantially all&rdquo; is defined in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="53.4942(b)-1" subref="(c)">26 C.F.R. &sect;53.4942(b)-1(c)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> The second test is actually a set of three tests, at least one of which must be met:</para.text>
<list list.style="para">
<list.item><name.block><designator>(1)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>Asset test, where substantially more than half of the assets must be devoted to the organization&apos;s exempt activities, a functionally related business, or stock of a controlled corporation devoted to those activities;</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>(2)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>Endowment test, where at least two-thirds of its annual expenditures for active work must equal two-thirds of its minimum investment return; and</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>(3)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>Support test, where the foundation&apos;s support must come from the public and from five or more organizations, none of which donated more than 25&percnt; of the support. The organizations must not be controlled by the foundation. No more than half the support can come from investment income.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4942" subref="(j)" pararef="(3)" spararef="(B)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4942(j)(3)(B)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Operating foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7713 to D-7715" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7713 to D-7715</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Operating foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:116">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:116</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para></list.item>
</list></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>Once those laborious qualifications are met, a private operating foundation may enjoy five benefits not available to nonoperating foundations. First, donors may contribute and deduct up to 50&percnt; of their income to the foundation instead of the 30&percnt; maximum permitted for contributions to other foundations.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="170" subref="(b)" pararef="(1)" spararef="(E)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;170(b)(1)(E)</cite>. Pooled fund foundations and foundations that distribute corpus are also entitled to the 50&percnt; amount even if not operating foundations.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Second, certain &ldquo;old-line&rdquo; foundations may avoid the tax on investment income.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4940" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4940(d)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Organizations qualifying as exempt operating foundations for purposes of excise tax on investment income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7505">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-7505</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Operating foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:116">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:116</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> These foundations must have been publicly supported for at least 10 years or else qualified on January 1, 1983; at least 75&percnt; of the governing body must not be disqualified persons; the governing body must represent the general public; and no officer of the foundation can be a disqualified person. Third, the minimum payout requirements imposed on private foundations do not apply because they have been replaced by the income test requirements discussed above. Fourth, the requirement that a grant from a private foundation must be expended within one year does not apply.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4942" subref="(g)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4942(g)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Fifth, the tax on self-dealing imposed on private foundations does not apply to private operating foundations.<footnote><footnote.reference>12</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4942" subref="(a)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4942(a)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>To be exempt from taxation of its net investment income under <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-irc" titleref="26" secref="4940">Section 4940 of the Internal Revenue Code</cite>, an operating foundation must also establish that: (1) it has been publicly supported for at least 10 taxable years; (2) at all times during the tax year in question, the governing body of the organization consisted of individuals, at least 75&percnt; of whom were not disqualified, and was broadly representative of the general public; and (3) the foundation at no time during the taxable year had an officer who is a disqualified individual.<footnote><footnote.reference>13</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4940" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4940(d)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>For a discussion of disqualified persons, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:18">&sect;31:18</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Operating foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7713 to D-7715" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7713 to D-7715</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Operating foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:116">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:116</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>&ldquo;Qualifying distributions&rdquo; are defined as amounts paid to accomplish or to acquire assets used directly in carrying out one or more charitable purposes other than contributions to: (1) organizations controlled by the foundation or by one or more &ldquo;disqualified persons&rdquo;;<footnote><footnote.reference>14</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>For the definition of &ldquo;disqualified persons,&rdquo; see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:18">&sect;31:18</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Qualified distributions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7706 to D-7710" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7706 to D-7710</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Distribution of income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:111, 10:111" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:111, 10:111</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> or (2) to private nonoperating foundations unless such organizations or foundations make qualifying distributions to recipients other than nonoperating foundations in an amount equal to the contribution received within one year of the receipt thereof.<footnote><footnote.reference>15</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4942" subref="(g)" pararef="(1), (3)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4942(g)(1), (3)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text>The minimum investment return for any private foundation for any taxable year is 5&percnt; of the excess of: (1) the aggregate fair market value of all assets of the foundation, other than those which are used (or held for use) directly in carrying out the foundation&apos;s exempt purpose over (2) the acquisition indebtedness with respect to such assets.<footnote><footnote.reference>16</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|17|31:17"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4942" subref="(e)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4942(e)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Taxes on failure to distribute income; minimum investment return, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7700 to D-7702" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7700 to D-7702</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:18</designator><name>Definitions<sep/>Disqualified person; substantial contributor</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>A &ldquo;disqualified person&rdquo; is defined by statute<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4946" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4946(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>There is a separate definition of &ldquo;disqualified individual&rdquo; for purposes of the tax on income of a foundation, which includes only substantial contributors and owners of the foundation as described below. See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4940" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4940(d)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disqualified persons defined, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-8101">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-8101</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disqualified person transactions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:108 to 10:110" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:108 to 10:110</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> as:</para.text>
<list list.style="para">
<list.item><name.block><designator>1</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>A substantial contributor to the foundation.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>2</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>A foundation manager.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>3</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>An owner of more than 20&percnt; of: (a) the voting power of a corporation; (b) the profits interest of a partnership; or (c) the beneficial interest of a trust or unincorporated enterprise, which is a substantial contributor to the foundation.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>4</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>A member of the family of any individual described in 1 to 3 above.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>5</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>A corporation in which persons described in 1 to 4, above, own more than 35&percnt; of the voting power.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>6</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>A partnership in which persons described in 1 to 4, above, own more than 35&percnt; of the profit interest.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>7</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>A trust or estate in which persons described in 1 to 4, above, hold more than 35&percnt; of the beneficial interest.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>8</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>For purposes of the tax on excess business holdings only,<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4943">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4943</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disqualified persons defined, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-8101">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-8101</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disqualified person transactions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:108 to 10:110" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:108 to 10:110</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> a private foundation that is effectively controlled by the same persons who control the private foundation in question or a private foundation deriving substantially all of its contributions from the same persons who made substantially all of the contributions to the foundation in question.</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>9</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>For purposes of the tax on self-dealing only,<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4941">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4941</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Government officials as limited disqualified persons, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-8103">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-8103</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disqualified person transactions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:108 to 10:110" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:108 to 10:110</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> a government official.</para.text></para></list.item>
</list></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>A &ldquo;substantial contributor&rdquo; means any person contributing or bequeathing an aggregate amount of more than &dollar;5000 to the foundation if such amount is more than 2&percnt; of the total contributions and bequests received by the foundation for the taxable year in which the contribution or bequest is received. It also means the creator of a trust.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="507" subref="(d)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;507(d)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disqualified persons defined, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-8101">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-8101</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Disqualified person transactions, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:108 to 10:110" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:108 to 10:110</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text>Self-dealing does not include a transaction between a private foundation and a disqualified person where the disqualified person status arises only as a result of the transaction.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|18|31:18"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="53.4941(d)-1" subref="(a)">26 C.F.R. &sect;53.4941(d)-1(a)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:19</designator><name>Tax consequences of private foundation status</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>Classification as a private foundation has many tax ramifications. The foundation is not exempt from income taxes,<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="508" subref="(e)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;508(e)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Taxation of private foundations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7201">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-7201</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> and donations to the foundation are generally not deductible by the donor.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="508" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;508(d)</cite>. A deduction is permitted in certain circumstances. See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="170" subref="(b)" pararef="(1)" spararef="(E)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;170(b)(1)(E)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Deductibility of gifts of private foundation donee, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:133">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:133</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>Additionally, private foundations are subject to a variety of special taxes that are not imposed on other exempt organizations.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><ital>Termination tax</ital>. A termination tax applies to a private foundation that is guilty of willful action or inaction that is subject to tax under one of the provisions discussed below. Because of the confiscatory nature of the tax, the organization is terminated by the IRS. However, the tax cannot exceed the smaller of all tax benefits received by the organization because of its exempt status or the total value of the assets of the organization.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="507" subref="(c)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;507(c)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>For a discussion of the termination of private foundation status, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:24">&sect;31:24</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> If state officials take over the assets for a charitable purpose, the IRS can abate the tax.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.507-9">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.507-9</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Tax on termination of private foundation status, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7228 to D-7234" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7228 to D-7234</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Termination of foundation, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:118">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:118</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>The tax can, theoretically, apply to any change in status, including dissolution or a transfer of all assets to another private foundation. The regulations, however, provide methods for avoiding the tax for transfers and liquidations that comply with a charitable use of the assets.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.507-1">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.507-1</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><ital>Self-dealing tax</ital>. A tax is imposed on dealings by a disqualified person with a private foundation.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4941" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4941(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>For a definition of &ldquo;disqualified persons,&rdquo; see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:18">&sect;31:18</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Self-dealing taxes, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7600 to D-7620" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7600 to D-7620</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Expenditure penalty, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:113 to 10:115" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:113 to 10:115</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The tax is initially 10&percnt; of the amount of the transaction but increases to 200&percnt; if the transaction is not reversed. The tax also applies to a foundation manager but is limited to 5&percnt; (50&percnt; on failure to reverse), with a maximum tax of &dollar;20,000. Self-dealing includes sales, leases, loans, and other transactions.<footnote><footnote.reference>7</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4941" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4941(d)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>A disqualified person is one who owns more than 20&percnt; of the stock, who manages the operation, or who is a substantial contributor to the organization.<footnote><footnote.reference>8</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4946" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4946(a)</cite>. Family members of these persons along with trusts, partnerships, and corporations associated with them are included as disqualified persons.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> A substantial contributor is one who contributes more than &dollar;5,000 if that amount is more than 2&percnt; of the total contributions.<footnote><footnote.reference>9</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="507" subref="(d)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;507(d)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> If the organization is a trust, the creator of the trust is a substantial contributor even if his or her contribution is less than &dollar;5,000. Governmental employees are also included as disqualified persons.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>An exception exists for such actions as making an interest-free loan to the organization or furnishing goods or services used by the foundation for its exempt activities.<footnote><footnote.reference>10</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4941" subref="(d)" pararef="(2)" spararef="(B)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4941(d)(2)(B)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><ital>Undistributed income tax</ital>. If a foundation does not distribute a minimum amount to charity each year, nominally 5&percnt; of assets, it is subject to an initial 30&percnt; tax on income that should have been distributed.<footnote><footnote.reference>11</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4942" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4942(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Tax on failures to distribute income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" topicname="Exempt Organizations" parmkref="D-7700 to D-7728" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA), Exempt Organizations &dblpara;D-7700 to D-7728</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Distribution of income, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:111, 10:112" secrange="y">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &dblsect;10:111, 10:112</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> If the violation is not remedied, the tax rises to 100&percnt;. The assets upon which the calculation is made are reduced by any acquisition indebtedness and by the value of assets used to perform the exempt functions of the foundation.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><ital>Excess business holdings tax</ital>. A tax of 10&percnt; is levied on excess business holdings of a foundation.<footnote><footnote.reference>12</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4943" subref="(a)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4943(a)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Tax on excess business holdings, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" topicname="Exempt Organizations" parmkref="D-7800 to D-7826" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA), Exempt Organizations &dblpara;D-7800 to D-7826</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Tax on foundation assets, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:104">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:104</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> If these are not divested, the tax can increase to 200&percnt;.<footnote><footnote.reference>13</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4943" subref="(b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4943(b)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Excess business holdings are those of the foundation and its disqualified persons that exceed 20&percnt; of a company. When the company is controlled by unrelated persons, the allowable amount increases to 35&percnt;. A foundation can hold up to 2&percnt; of a company, whatever the holdings of disqualified persons.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><ital>Jeopardy investments tax</ital>. A 10&percnt; tax is imposed on both a foundation and its manager on any investment that jeopardizes a foundation&apos;s exempt purpose.<footnote><footnote.reference>14</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4944" subref="(a)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4944(a)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private foundation investments that jeopardize charitable purposes, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" topicname="Exempt Organizations" parmkref="D-7900 to D-7911" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA), Exempt Organizations &dblpara;D-7900 to D-7911</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The Code, in effect, imposes its own prudent investor rule on foundation investments. Under the Treasury regulations, an investment will be considered to jeopardize the carrying out of the exempt purposes of a private foundation if it is determined that the foundation managers, in making the investment, have failed to exercise ordinary business care and prudence, under the facts and circumstances prevailing at the time of making the investment, in providing for the long- and short-term financial needs of the foundation to carry out its exempt purposes. In the exercise of the requisite standard of care and prudence, the foundation managers may take into account the expected return (including both income and appreciation of capital), the risks of rising and falling price levels, and the need for diversification within the investment portfolio (for example, with respect to type of security, type of industry, maturity of company, degree of risk, and potential for return). The determination whether the investment of a particular amount jeopardizes the carrying out of the exempt purposes of a foundation shall be made on an investment-by-investment basis, in each case taking into account the foundation&apos;s portfolio as a whole.<footnote><footnote.reference>15</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="53.4944-1" subref="(a)" pararef="(2)" spararef="(i)">26 C.F.R. &sect;53.4944-1(a)(2)(i)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> The tax can rise to 25&percnt; on the foundation, with an additional 5&percnt; on the manager.<footnote><footnote.reference>16</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4944" subref="(b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4944(b)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Assets related to the exempt purpose of the organization are not included as a jeopardy investment even if no income or appreciation is expected.<footnote><footnote.reference>17</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4944" subref="(c)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4944(c)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> An example is land and building for a church.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><ital>Legislative activities tax</ital>. A tax is imposed on expenditures made to influence legislation, to sway the outcome of an election, or to engage in a voter-registration drive.<footnote><footnote.reference>18</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4945" subref="(d), (e)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4945(d), (e)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Tax on expenditures attempting to influence legislation, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-8004, D-8005" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-8004, D-8005</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> The initial tax is 20&percnt;, and this can rise to 100&percnt; of the expenditure if it is not reversed.<footnote><footnote.reference>19</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4945" subref="(a), (b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4945(a), (b)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> A manager is initially taxed 5&percnt;, rising to 50&percnt;.<footnote><footnote.reference>20</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4945" subref="(a), (b)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4945(a), (b)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><ital>Prohibited grants tax</ital>. Certain grants by a foundation are subject to the same tax as that imposed on prohibited legislative activities.<footnote><footnote.reference>21</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="4945" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;4945(d)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Tax on prohibited grants, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-8009 to D-8019" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-8009 to D-8019</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> These include grants made:</para.text>
<list list.style="para">
<list.item><name.block><designator>(1)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>to an individual for travel or study unless the grant is made on a nondiscriminatory basis;</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>(2)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>to a private foundation unless the grantor makes sure the foundation uses the grant properly;</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>(3)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>to an exempt operating foundation (discussed below) that is not subject to the duty to make sure a grant is not properly used; and</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>(4)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>to anyone for a purpose other than an exempt purpose.</para.text></para></list.item>
</list></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text>Under New York law, an entity classified as a private foundation is required to take the acts necessary to avoid excise taxes being imposed on the corporation.<footnote><footnote.reference>22</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|19|31:19"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-ny-law-notforprofitcorp" secref="406" subref="(a)">N-PCL &sect;406(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Specific Requirements of the not-for-profit corporation law, see <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="71">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;71</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> However, there are no state taxes imposed on such transactions.</para.text></para>
</section.body>
</section>
<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:20</designator><name>Returns and reporting requirements</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text>Like most charitable organizations, private foundations must file annual returns.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6033" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6033(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text>The tax on net investment income is returned on <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-form" numref="990-PF">IRS Form 990-PF</cite>. All other taxes, such as those on self-dealing, undistributed income, and political expenditures, are reported on <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-irs-form" numref="4720">IRS Form 4720</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text>For a discussion of the return requirements for exempt organizations, generally, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:12">&sect;31:12</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private foundation returns, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="S-2860 to S-2862" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;S-2860 to S-2862</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Failure to file annual returns may result in the imposition of penalties.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6652" subref="(c)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6652(c)(1)</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text>A private foundation is required to include in its annual return the names and addresses of foundation managers and certain additional information concerning contributions and stock holdings, an income statement, a balance sheet, a schedule of securities and other assets held by the foundation at the close of the taxable year, and a schedule of grants and contributions paid or proof for payment during the taxable year.<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6033" subref="(c)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6033(c)(1)</cite>; <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.6033-3">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.6033-3</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private foundation returns, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="S-2860 to S-2862" parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;S-2860 to S-2862</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text>It is further required that all foundations subject to the reporting requirements publish a notice as to the availability for inspection of their annual return within a statutorily specified period from the date of publication.<footnote><footnote.reference>4</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6104" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6104(d)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text>A copy of the notice and proof of its publication must be filed with the foundation&apos;s return. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6033" subref="(c)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6033(c)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Annual reporting by not-for-profit organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="378">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;378</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Annual reporting by charitable organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Charities" secref="87">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Charities &sect;87</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Annual financial or other reports, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Corporations" secref="278">Am. Jur. 2d, Corporations &sect;278</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> Failure to meet the public inspection requirements may result in the imposition of penalties.<footnote><footnote.reference>5</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6652">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6652</cite>.</para.text></para></footnote.body></footnote> Foundation managers are additionally required to furnish copies of the annual return to such state officials at such times and under such conditions as regulations require.<footnote><footnote.reference>6</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|20|31:20"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="6033" subref="(c)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;6033(c)(2)</cite>; <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.6033-3">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.6033-3</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Annual reporting by not-for-profit organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Business Relationships" secref="378">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Business Relationships &sect;378</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Annual reporting by charitable organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="nyj2" topicname="Charities" secref="87">N.Y. Jur. 2d, Charities &sect;87</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Annual financial or other reports, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="aj2" topicname="Corporations" secref="278">Am. Jur. 2d, Corporations &sect;278</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>

<section>
<section.front>
<outline.name.block><label>&sect;</label><designator>31:21</designator><name>Qualifying for exemption from the foundation rules</name></outline.name.block>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text><cite type="topic.key" normalpub="key" sub="Internal Revenue" numref="4045 to 4079" numrange="y">West&apos;s Key Number Digest, Internal Revenue &key;4045 to 4079</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block>
</section.front>
<section.body>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text>Private foundations include all charitable organizations, other than those exempted by statute.<footnote><footnote.reference>1</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="509" subref="(a)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;509(a)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text>For a definition of charitable organizations, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:2">&sect;31:2</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text>For a list of exempt organizations, see <cite type="secondaryxref" secref="31:3">&sect;31:3</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Presumption that exempt organization is private foundation, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7200">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-7200</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote> In determining whether to grant exemption from private foundation status under Sections 509(a)(1) or 509(a)(2), the basic consideration is whether the organization&apos;s structure, proposed programs or activities, and intended method of operation are such as to attract the type of broadly based support from the general public, public charities, and governmental units necessary to meet the organization&apos;s support requirements.<footnote><footnote.reference>2</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text><cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.509(a)-3" subref="(d)" pararef="(2)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.509(a)-3(d)(2)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text>The support requirements concern mainly the sources of the organization&apos;s financing. <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="509" subref="(d)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;509(d)</cite>. The factors used in determining whether an organization is exempt under <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="509" subref="(a)" pararef="(1)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;509(a)(1)</cite> as a &ldquo;Section 170(b)(1)(A)(vi) organization&rdquo; are set out in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.170A-9" subref="(f)">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.170A-9(f)</cite>. The factors in determining whether an organization is exempt under <cite type="lrre" normalpub="statute-us-code" titleref="26" secref="509" subref="(a)" pararef="(2)">26 U.S.C.A. &sect;509(a)(2)</cite> are set out in <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.509(a)-3">26 C.F.R. &sect;1.509(a)-3</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Churches, schools, hospitals, etc., government-supported charities, and governmental units, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7203">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-7203</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Broadly supported organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7204 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7204 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private foundations defined, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:101">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:101</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text></para>
<para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text>In addition to the sources of the organization&apos;s financing, pertinent factors in determining the character of the organization include:<footnote><footnote.reference>3</footnote.reference><footnote.body><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text>Some different factors may be pertinent when an organization seeks to show that it is exempt under Section 170(b)(1)(A)(vi) and thus comes within Section 509(a)(1), and when an organization seeks to establish exemption under Section 509(a)(2). See <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.170A-9" subref="(f)">26 C.F.R. &dblsect;1.170A-9(f)</cite>, <cite type="lrre" normalpub="exec-us-cfr" titleref="26" secref="1.509(a)-3" subref="(d)" pararef="(3)">1.509(a)-3(d)(3)</cite>.</para.text></para>
<research.reference.block>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Churches, schools, hospitals, etc., government supported charities and governmental units, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7203">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &para;D-7203</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Broadly supported organizations, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftc2" parmkref="D-7204 et seq." parmkrange="y">Federal Tax Coordinator 2d (RIA) &dblpara;D-7204 et seq.</cite></ref.text></reference.entry>
<reference.entry><ref.text>Private foundations defined, <cite type="secondary" normalpub="ftglf" secref="10:101">Federal Tax Guide to Legal Forms &sect;10:101</cite>.</ref.text></reference.entry>
</research.reference.block></footnote.body></footnote></para.text>
<list list.style="para">
<list.item><name.block><designator>(1)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text>whether the organization has or will have a governing body comprised of public officials, persons chosen by public officials, community leaders, or persons having special knowledge of a particular relevant field;</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>(2)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text>whether a substantial portion of the initial funding is to be provided by the general public, public charities, or government grants;</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>(3)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text>in the case of an organization that carries on fundraising activities, whether concrete plans have been made for solicitation of funds from the general public, whether any steps have been taken to implement such plan, whether any firm commitments have been obtained from exempt charities, and whether the organization has made any commitments to or established any working relationship with those organizations or classes of persons intended as future recipients; and</para.text></para></list.item>
<list.item><name.block><designator>(4)</designator></name.block><para ct.id="f477b8b0b92511efa86bc22ba615bad8|21|31:21"><para.text>whether the organization is or will be required to make its services, facilities, performances, or products available to the general public on a continuing basis.</para.text></para></list.item>
</list></para>
</section.body>
